Character and Scholarly Praise of Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani
Biography of Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani with character and praises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the personal attributes of Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, the nature of his seclusion, and the high esteem in which he was held by his scholarly peers.

Core Idea
True piety can be misunderstood, but a scholar's character is witnessed by his students.

This passage introduces us to Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, the commentator on Jawharat al-Tawhid. Before diving into his theological work, it is valuable to know the man: his bold yet gentle character, his awe-inspiring teaching style, and the controversy over his seclusion. The passage then records glowing praises from several notable scholars, painting a picture of a revered master of multiple sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the two main sections: personal attributes and scholarly praises.
2
Identify personal attributes
Look for keywords like shahama (boldness), hayba (awe), and the description of his teaching atmosphere.
The phrase 'as if birds were on their heads' indicates extreme stillness and respect.
3
Examine the seclusion debate
Two interpretations of his seclusion are given: piety vs. laziness. The author affirms the first as correct.
This is a clear example of a misconception addressed directly in the text.
4
Review scholarly praises
Four scholars are quoted praising Laqqani. Note the specific fields they highlight, especially al-Hamawi's detailed list.
Each praise adds a dimension: mastery in hadith, inheritance of knowledge, and being an imam.

From his attributes: Biography of the commentary's author, the son of the author, Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani: He possessed boldness, severity, and awe. The senior shaykhs of his time respected his standing and valued his opinion. He was majestic and awe-inspiring among scholars and those below them, despite his good companionship and gentle nature. People in his lesson were as if birds were on their heads; none of those present could ask him or respond to him out of awe for him. When he spoke about an issue, he would dictate all that had been mentioned concerning it. When he presented a discussion, he left nothing unaddressed. al-Shaykh al-Ayyashi described him as being overcome by love of seclusion and aversion to people. Some said that was devotion and asceticism, others said it was laziness and boredom. The correct view—God willing—is the first. So he only taught during the three months: Rajab and its two followers, and most of his teaching then was hadith and the like. Praise of scholars for him: His student, the scholar Mustafa ibn Fath Allah al-Hamawi, said in his biography of him: 'Our shaykh, the Imam, the shaykh of hadith scholars in the Egyptian lands. He was skilled in hadith, knowledge of its defects and transmitters, a jurist in his school, an imam in the science of kalam and Arabic arts, gentle of character, good in discussion, excellent in lecture.' And al-Shaykh Abd Allah al-Ayyashi mentioned him in his travelogue, saying: 'He is the inheritor of his father's sciences, the unique one among his companions, who has no peer.' And al-Muhbi, the precise, proficient, insightful memorizer, the shaykh of the Malikis in his time in Cairo, said of him. And the scholar Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Mallawi said of him: 'The journey's destination, the imam, the great one, the result of the eminent scholars, our master al-Shaykh Abd al-Salam.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the commentator Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, beginning with his personal attributes and then moving to scholarly praises. First, it describes his character: he was bold, severe, and awe-inspiring, yet gentle. In his lessons, students were extremely still and quiet due to awe. He would thoroughly cover topics. Al-Ayyashi reports that he loved seclusion and avoided people, with some attributing this to piety and others to laziness; the author affirms it was piety. He only taught during Rajab, Sha'ban, and Ramadan, focusing on hadith. Then specific praises are quoted: al-Hamawi emphasizes his mastery of hadith, fiqh, kalam, and Arabic, and his good character; al-Ayyashi calls him the inheritor of his father's knowledge and unique; al-Muhbi praises him as a precise scholar; al-Mallawi calls him the ultimate destination in learning and a great imam.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people thought Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani's seclusion was due to laziness and boredom.
Correction: The correct view, as affirmed in the passage, is that his seclusion was an act of devotion and asceticism (تَنسُكٌ وزهادةٌ).

Key Takeaway
Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani was a revered scholar whose seclusion was a mark of piety, and he was praised by numerous scholars for his mastery in hadith, fiqh, kalam, and Arabic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to be misunderstood by others for the sake of your devotion to Allah, as al-Laqqani was? Or do you seek the approval of people even when it compromises your religious commitments?
?
Al-Laqqani was both awe-inspiring and gentle. Which of these qualities do you lack in your relationships, and how can you cultivate the other without losing your integrity?
?
The scholars praised al-Laqqani. If you were to die today, what would your students or peers say about you? Does that align with what Allah knows about you?

Ibn al-Nazim al-Laqqani: Biography and Key Works
Biography of the commentator with list of works and death details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly contributions of Ibn al-Nazim 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, including his major commentaries on his father's theological poem and the clarification regarding the number of his works on the Jawhara.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Nazim's commentaries shaped the study of his father's creed.

This passage introduces us to the commentator Ibn al-Nazim al-Laqqani, whose works on his father's theological poem are central to the Ash'ari tradition. We will learn about his most famous commentaries and clarify a common confusion about the third work on the Jawhara. The passage also records his death and the sources of his biography.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical opening
Notice how al-Laqqani is introduced as 'the eminent, the outcome of the great scholars'. This sets the tone for his scholarly stature.
He is called 'Ibn al-Nazim' meaning 'son of the poet', referring to his father who authored the poem.
2
Identify the two main commentaries
Find Irshad al-Murid (the abridged commentary) and Ithaf al-Murid (the current book). Note the completion date of Ithaf al-Murid: 20 Ramadan 1047 AH.
Ithaf al-Murid is the most famous and widely spread of his works.
3
Understand the clarification about the third work
The biographer addresses a claim that al-Laqqani wrote three commentaries on al-Jawhara. He clarifies that the third is actually a gloss on his father's intermediate commentary, not a full commentary.
This resolution shows the importance of precise attribution.
4
Review the remaining works and death
Scan the list of other works (4-8) and note the death details: Friday 26 Shawwal 1078 AH, funeral at al-Azhar led by Ali al-Shabramallisī.
A variant date is mentioned but the biographer prefers his student's account.

شرحه هذا يوم الخميس لعشرين خلت من شهر رمضان المعظم، سنة: (١٠٤٧هـ) فتأليفه له بعد وفاة والده بـ ٦ سنوات تقريبا .
٣ - ذكر الشيخ مصطفى بن فتح الله الحموي في ترجمته له في «فوائد الارتحال قال: (له ثلاثة شروح على عقيدة والده الجوهرة) ولم أقف على هذا الثالث ولا على اسمه، وبعضهم ذكر أن اسمه: «فتح المجيد بكفاية أنَّ المريد والظاهر أنه سهو ، فهذا هو اسم شرح له على نظم «الجزائرية» والذي يظهر لي أنَّ سبب إطلاقهم أنَّ له ثلاثة شروح على الجوهرة.. هو أن له فعلا ثلاثة أعمال على جوهرة والده ، منهما شرحاه السابق ذكرهما ، وله عمل ثالث وهو حاشية على شرح والده المتوسط «هداية المريد» سماه: «فتح الوصيد لهداية «المريد وبذلك تحقق لنا أنه له شرحين وحاشية على شرح والده.
٤ ـ له شرحان على المنظومة الجزائرية» أحدهما كبير والآخر مختصر ، كذا ذكره الشيخ الحموي في ترجمته له في فوائد الارتحال»، وفي المكتبة الأزهرية عدة نسخ من مخطوطات فتح المجيد بكفاية «المريد وهو شرح لطيف على المنظومة الجزائرية المُسماة : كفاية المريد وحلية العبيد»

ترجمة صاحب الشرح ابن الناظم عبد السلام اللقاني
للشيخ العارف أحمد الزواوي، والتي شرحها أيضا قبله الإمام السنوسي الله جميعا ، ولم أقف على خبر الشرح الثاني .
رحمهم
المختار
٥ - ابتسام الأزهار من رياض الأخيار في ربيع الأبرار بمولد الحبيب
٦ ـ وله حاشية على شرح الصدور للحافظ السيوطي. ودرسه في مجالسه بالجامع الفاكهاني .
۷ - وحاشية على تذكرة القرطبي وقد درس كتاب «التذكرة» في مجالسه بالجامع الأزهر.
۸ - السراج الوهاج بشرح قصتني الاسراء والمعراج وغيرها من الرسائل والمؤلفات النافعة .
وفاته:
(۱) توفي الله يوم الجمعة ، في السادس والعشرين (1) من شوال ، سنة ثمانٍ وسبعين بعد الألف (۱۰۷۸ هـ ) وصلي عليه يوم السبت بالجامع الأزهر ، وأم الناس في صلاة الجنازة العلامة خاتمة المحققين علي الشبرملسي الشافعي صاحب الحاشية المشهورة على نهاية المحتاج ـ وكان مشهدا عظيما، رحمه الله تعالى ونفعنا به (۲).
هو
(۱) وعند المحبي في خلاصة الأثر أنه توفي يوم الجمعة في خامس عشر شوال ، ولعل الصواب ما أثبته تلميذه الذي حضر جنازته وصلى عليه. (۲) مصادر الترجمة فوائد الارتحال ونتائج السفر في أخبار القرن الحادي عشر للعلامة مصطفى الحموي و اخلاصة الأثر في أعيان القرن الحادي عشر للعلامة المحبي. و«اليواقيت الثمينة».
Translation of the author of the commentary, Ibn al-Nāẓim 'Abd al-Salām al-Laqqānī. The eminent, the outcome of the great scholars, our master Shaykh 'Abd al-Salām. Among his works: 1. Irshād al-Murīd bi-Sharḥ Jawhar al-Tawḥīd – which is his abridged commentary. 2. Ithāf al-Murīd bi-Sharḥ Jawharat al-Tawḥīd – which is this our book, and it is the one that became famous, spread, and showed signs of acceptance and blessing, and he stated that he completed its composition on Thursday, the twentieth of the noble month of Ramaḍān, year 1047 AH; its authorship was about six years after the death of his father. 3. Shaykh Muṣṭafā ibn Fatḥ Allāh al-Ḥamawī mentioned in his biography of him in 'Fawā'id al-Irtiḥāl': 'He has three commentaries on his father's creed, al-Jawhara.' I have not come across this third one nor its name. Some mentioned that its name is 'Fatḥ al-Majīd bi-Kifāyat al-Murīd' but apparently it is a mistake, for this is the name of a commentary on the 'al-Jazā'iriyya' poem. What appears to me is that the reason they say he has three commentaries on al-Jawhara is that he indeed has three works on his father's Jawhara: two commentaries previously mentioned, and a third work which is a gloss on his father's intermediate commentary 'Hidāyat al-Murīd' named 'Fatḥ al-Waṣīd li-Hidāyat al-Murīd'. Thus it is established for us that he has two commentaries and a gloss on his father's commentary. 4. He has two commentaries on the 'al-Manẓūma al-Jazā'iriyya': one large and one concise. Thus mentioned Shaykh al-Ḥamawī in his biography in 'Fawā'id al-Irtiḥāl'. In the Azhar Library there are several manuscript copies of 'Fatḥ al-Majīd bi-Kifāyat al-Murīd', which is a nice commentary on the 'al-Manẓūma al-Jazā'iriyya' named 'Kifāyat al-Murīd wa Ḥilyat al-'Abīd', by the knower of God Shaykh Aḥmad al-Zawāwī, and which Imām al-Sanūsī also commented on before him – may God have mercy on them all – and I have not come across news of the second commentary. 5. Ibtisām al-Azhār min Riyāḍ al-Akhyār fī Rabī' al-Abrār bi-Mawlid al-Ḥabīb. 6. He has a gloss on 'Sharḥ al-Ṣudūr' by al-Ḥāfiẓ al-Suyūṭī, and he taught it in his sessions at al-Jāmi' al-Fakkāhānī. 7. And a gloss on 'Tadhkirat al-Qurṭubī', and he taught the book 'al-Tadhkira' in his sessions at al-Azhar Mosque. 8. al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj bi-Sharḥ Qaṣṣatay al-Isrā' wa al-Mi'rāj, and other beneficial treatises and compositions. His death: (1) He died – may God have mercy on him – on Friday, the twenty-sixth of Shawwāl, year 1078 AH, and the funeral prayer was performed for him on Saturday at al-Azhar Mosque. Leading the people in the funeral prayer was the scholar, the seal of the verifiers, 'Alī al-Shabramallisī al-Shāfi'ī, author of the famous gloss on Nihāyat al-Muḥtāj. It was a great scene. May God Almighty have mercy on him and benefit us with him. (1) According to al-Muḥibbī in 'Khulāṣat al-Athar', he died on Friday, the fifteenth of Shawwāl. But the correct seems to be what his student who attended his funeral and prayed over him recorded. (2) Sources of the biography: Fawā'id al-Irtiḥāl and Natā'ij al-Safar fī Akhbār al-Qarn al-Ḥādī 'Ashar by the scholar Muṣṭafā al-Ḥamawī, and Khulāṣat al-Athar fī A'yān al-Qarn al-Ḥādī 'Ashar by the scholar al-Muḥibbī, and al-Yawāqīt al-Thamīna.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry (tarjama) for the author of the commentary, Ibn al-Nāẓim 'Abd al-Salām al-Laqqānī. It begins by praising him as 'the eminent, the outcome of the great scholars'. Then it lists his works in numbered order. The first work is 'Irshād al-Murīd', an abridged commentary on his father's poem. The second is 'Ithāf al-Murīd', which is the current book; the author notes that it was completed in Ramaḍān 1047 AH, about six years after his father's death. The third item discusses a claim by al-Ḥamawī that al-Laqqānī wrote three commentaries on his father's 'Jawhara'. The biographer (the editor of this book) clarifies that the third work is actually a gloss (ḥāshiya) on his father's intermediate commentary 'Hidāyat al-Murīd', titled 'Fatḥ al-Waṣīd'. Thus he had two commentaries and one gloss. The fourth item states he wrote two commentaries on the 'al-Manẓūma al-Jazā'iriyya' (one large, one concise) and mention is made of manuscripts in the Azhar Library. The fifth item is 'Ibtisām al-Azhār' on the Prophet's birth. The sixth is a gloss on al-Suyūṭī's 'Sharḥ al-Ṣudūr'. The seventh is a gloss on al-Qurṭubī's 'Tadhkira'. The eighth is 'al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj' on the Night Journey and Ascension. Then the death notice: he died on Friday, 26 Shawwāl 1078 AH (with a variant date from al-Muḥibbī), and his funeral was at al-Azhar, led by 'Alī al-Shabramallisī. The passage closes with sources for the biography. The overall structure is a standard biographical notice with a numbered list of works and death details.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ibn al-Nazim wrote three full commentaries on his father's Jawhara (al-Jawhara).
Correction: The biographer clarifies that the third work is actually a gloss (hasheya) on his father's intermediate commentary 'Hidāyat al-Murīd', not a full commentary. Thus he wrote two commentaries and one gloss.

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Nazim al-Laqqani wrote two main commentaries on his father's Jawhara (with a third being a gloss) and many other works; he died in 1078 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn al-Nazim spent years after his father's death to produce a clear commentary on his creed. What core belief about Allah have you inherited from your upbringing, and how are you actively studying it to pass it on to the next generation?
?
He wrote multiple works to remove confusion (e.g., clarifying the third work is a gloss). Are you content with superficial understanding of your faith, or do you dig deep to resolve ambiguities? What one specific area of 'aqida will you study in depth this week to clarify your own heart?
?

Biography of 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqani
Biographical entry listing works and death of al-Laqani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, works, and death of 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqani, the commentator of Jawharat al-Tawhid.

Core Idea
Al-Laqani's works and scholarly legacy are a bridge to understanding the tradition of kalam commentary.

Before delving into the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid, it is useful to know the context of its commentator, 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqani. This biographical note provides a glimpse into his scholarly output and the circumstances of his passing, grounding the student in the personal history behind the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: it begins with identification, then lists works, then records death.
The passage is from a biographical dictionary or lesson introduction.
2
Identify the works listed
Focus on the numbered items (5-8). Identify the titles and subjects of each work. Note that the passage mentions a 'selection' (المختار) before the list.
These works reflect al-Laqani's range: hadith, sira, tafsir, and prophetic miracles.
3
Note the scholars mentioned
The passage mentions al-Zawawi and al-Sanusi as previous commentators, and al-Shabramallisi as leading his funeral. These connections place al-Laqani in a network of scholars.
This shows the continuity of scholarly tradition.
4
Reflect on the significance of his death
Consider the date (1078 AH) and the location (al-Azhar). Why might it be important that his funeral prayer was led by a prominent scholar?
This indicates his high status in the scholarly community.

ترجمة صاحب الشرح ابن الناظم عبد السلام اللقاني
للشيخ العارف أحمد الزواوي، والتي شرحها أيضا قبله الإمام السنوسي رحمهم الله جميعا ، ولم أقف على خبر الشرح الثاني .
المختار
٥ - ابتسام الأزهار من رياض الأخيار في ربيع الأبرار بمولد الحبيب
٦ ـ وله حاشية على شرح الصدور للحافظ السيوطي. ودرسه في مجالسه بالجامع الفاكهاني .
۷ - وحاشية على تذكرة القرطبي وقد درس كتاب «التذكرة» في مجالسه بالجامع الأزهر.
۸ - السراج الوهاج بشرح قصتي الإسراء والمعراج وغيرها من الرسائل والمؤلفات النافعة .
وفاته:
توفي رحمه الله يوم الجمعة ، في السادس والعشرين من شوال ، سنة ثمانٍ وسبعين بعد الألف (۱۰۷۸ هـ ) وصلي عليه يوم السبت بالجامع الأزهر ، وأم الناس في صلاة الجنازة العلامة خاتمة المحققين علي الشبرملسي الشافعي صاحب الحاشية المشهورة على نهاية المحتاج ـ وكان مشهدا عظيما، رحمه الله تعالى ونفعنا به.
Translation of the author of the commentary, Ibn al-Nadhim 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqani. By the gnostic shaykh Ahmad al-Zawawi, and which also before him Imam al-Sanusi commented on, may God have mercy on them all, and I did not come across news of the second commentary. The selection: 5 - Ibtisam al-Azhar min Riyad al-Akhyar fi Rabi' al-Abrar bi-Mawlid al-Habib. 6 - He has a gloss on Sharh al-Sudur by al-Hafiz al-Suyuti, and he studied it in his sessions at al-Jami' al-Fakahani. 7 - A gloss on Tadhkirat al-Qurtubi, and he studied the book 'al-Tadhkira' in his sessions at al-Jami' al-Azhar. 8 - al-Siraj al-Wahhaj bi-Sharh Qissatay al-Isra' wa-l-Mi'raj, and other beneficial treatises and works. His death: He died, may God have mercy on him, on Friday, the twenty-sixth of Shawwal, in the year one thousand and seventy-eight (1078 AH), and the funeral prayer was performed for him on Saturday at al-Jami' al-Azhar. The imam for the funeral prayer was the distinguished scholar, the seal of the verifiers, 'Ali al-Shabramallisi al-Shafi'i, author of the famous gloss on Nihayat al-Muhtaj — and it was a great scene. May God Almighty have mercy on him and benefit us with him.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical entry for 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqani, known as Ibn al-Nadhim, the author of the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid. It begins by noting that another commentary was written by Shaykh Ahmad al-Zawawi and earlier by Imam al-Sanusi, but the author (the biographer) has not found details on the second commentary. Then it lists eight of al-Laqani's works: the fifth is 'Ibtisam al-Azhar' on the birth of the Prophet; the sixth is a gloss on al-Suyuti's 'Sharh al-Sudur'; the seventh is a gloss on al-Qurtubi's 'Tadhkirah'; the eighth is 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' on the Night Journey and Ascension, among other beneficial works. Finally, it records his death: on Friday, 26 Shawwal 1078 AH, he passed away, and the funeral prayer was led by the prominent scholar 'Ali al-Shabramallisi at al-Azhar Mosque, with a large attendance. The entry concludes with a prayer for mercy.

Key Terms
ترجمة
شرح
ابن الناظم
وفاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage might lead a reader to think that al-Laqani authored the original Jawharat al-Tawhid poem.
Correction: Al-Laqani is the commentator (hence 'Ibn al-Nadhim'), not the original author. The original poem is by his father (or another). This passage is a biography of the commentator.

Biography of al-Amir al-Kabir: His Name, Lineage, and Early Life
Biographical details of al-Amir al-Kabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity and background of al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed, including his name, lineage, the origin of his title, his birth, and his early education.

Core Idea
A scholar's background reveals the roots of his authority.

Before we dive into the theological content of Sanusi's matn, it is valuable to know who the commentator on that matn was. This passage provides a brief biography of al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. By learning about his lineage, his title, and his early studies, we gain context for his scholarly contribution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, to get the full biographical account.
2
Identify the key details
Look for his full name, his hometown, the reason for his title 'al-Amir', his birth year, and his first teacher.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why knowing these details matters for understanding his work. Consider how his background shaped his scholarship.
This connects to the broader context of the text we are studying.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة العلامة الأمير الكبير صاحب «الحاشية على إتحاف المريد»
اسمه ونسبه:
هو العلامة الشيخ محمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن عبد القادر بن عبد العزيز بن محمد السَّنَباوي المالكي الأزهري الشهير بـ الأمير.
قال الجبرتي: أخبرني المُتَرجَمُ مِن لفظه أن أصلهم من المغرب، نزلوا بمصر عند سيدي عبد الوهاب أبي التخصيص، والتزموا بحصة بناحية «سَنْبو» وارتحلوا إليها وقطنوا بها ، وفيها ولد المترجم له .
من أين جاء لقب «الأمير»؟
الأمير هو لقب جده الأدنى أحمد، وسببه أن أحمد وأباه عبد القادر كان لهما إمرة بالصعيد فكان العلامة الأمير يلقب بالأمير الكبير، وولده محمد من بعده لقب بالأمير الصغير .
مولده ونشأته، وطلبه للعلم، وذكر بعض شيوخه.
ولد في شهر ذي الحجة سنة أربع وخمسين ومئة وألف (١١٥٤ هـ) أخذ القرآن وجوده على الشيخ محمد بن حسن السمنودي المعروف بالمنير، وحُبِّب إليه طلب العلم ، وأول ما حفظ متن الآجرومية» وسمع سائر الصحيح
Translation of the distinguished scholar al-Amir al-Kabir, author of 'The Gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed'. His name and lineage: He is the distinguished scholar, the shaykh Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Qadir ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad al-Sanabawi al-Maliki al-Azhari, known as al-Amir. Al-Jabarti said: The subject of this biography told me directly that their origin was from the Maghreb; they settled in Egypt at the residence of Sayyidi 'Abd al-Wahhab Abu al-Takhsis, and they took a share in the district of 'Sanbu', and they moved there and settled there, and therein the subject of this biography was born. Where did the title 'al-Amir' come from? Al-Amir is the title of his immediate grandfather Ahmad, and the reason is that Ahmad and his father 'Abd al-Qadir had a command (imrah) in the Sa'id region, so the distinguished scholar al-Amir was called al-Amir al-Kabir (the Great Amir), and his son Muhammad after him was called al-Amir al-Saghir (the Little Amir). His birth, upbringing, pursuit of knowledge, and mention of some of his teachers: He was born in the month of Dhu al-Hijjah in the year one thousand one hundred and fifty-four (1154 AH). He learned the Quran and its recitation under Shaykh Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Samnudi known as al-Munir, and the love of seeking knowledge was instilled in him. The first thing he memorized was the text of al-Ajurrumiyyah, and he heard all of the Sahih...
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins with his full name and lineage, tracing back to his great-grandfather. His family originally came from the Maghreb and settled in Egypt, eventually residing in the area of Sanbu, where he was born. The title 'al-Amir' is explained: it comes from his grandfather Ahmad and his father 'Abd al-Qadir, who held a military command (imrah) in Upper Egypt, so the scholar was known as al-Amir al-Kabir, and his son later as al-Amir al-Saghir. The entry then describes his birth in Dhul-Hijjah 1154 AH, his early Quranic studies under Shaykh Muhammad al-Samnudi, his love for knowledge, and his initial memorization of the famous grammar text al-Ajurrumiyyah. The biography ends mid-sentence noting that he heard all of Sahih (likely al-Bukhari or Muslim).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage says the love of seeking knowledge was 'instilled' in him. What steps are you actively taking to cultivate a genuine love for learning in your own life—not mere obligation? When your desire for knowledge wanes, what do you do to reignite that fire?

Biography of al-Amir al-Kabir: Lineage, Title, and Teachers
Biographical account of al-Amir al-Kabir, his name, lineage, title, birth, and studies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the background and scholarly training of al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of the commentary on Ithaaf al-Mureed.

Core Idea
Al-Amir al-Kabir's title reflects his family's administrative role, not royal lineage.

This lesson introduces the author of the annotation on Ithaaf al-Mureed, providing insight into his lineage, how he earned the title 'al-Amir', and his extensive education under notable scholars. Understanding his background helps appreciate the authority of his commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography thoroughly
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overall sense of al-Amir's life and scholarly journey.
2
Focus on the origin of the title 'al-Amir'
Notice that the passage clarifies the title comes from his grandfather's position as an amir in Upper Egypt, not from royal blood.
This corrects a common misconception.
3
Identify his most influential teacher
The passage emphasizes Shaykh Ali al-Saidi al-Adawi, whom al-Amir attended for over twenty years, calling him his primary source of benefit.
4
Survey the breadth of his studies
Make a mental list of the subjects and texts mentioned: Quran, hadith, fiqh, kalam, logic, astronomy, etc.
This shows his comprehensive training.

ترجمة العلامة الأمير الكبير صاحب «الحاشية على إتحاف المريد» • اسمه ونسبه: هو العلامة الشيخ محمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن عبد القادر بن عبد العزيز بن محمد السَّنَباوي المالكي الأزهري الشهير بـ الأمير . بـ: قال الجبرتي: أخبرني المُتَرجَمُ مِن لفظه أن أصلهم من المغرب، نزلوا بمصر عند سيدي عبد الوهاب أبي التخصيص، والتزموا بحصة بناحية «سَنْبو» وارتحلوا إليها وقطنوا بها ، وفيها ولد المترجم له . من أين جاء لقب «الأمير؟ الأمير هو لقب جده الأدنى أحمد، وسببه أن أحمد وأباه عبد القادر كان لهما إمرة بالصعيد فكان العلامة الأمير يلقب بالأمير الكبير، وولده محمد من بعده لقب بالأمير الصغير . مولده ونشأته، وطلبه للعلم، وذكر بعض شيوخه. ولد في شهر ذي الحجة سنة أربع وخمسين ومئة وألف (١١٥٤ هـ) أخذ القرآن وجوده على الشيخ محمد بن حسن السمنودي المعروف بالمنير، وحُبِّب إليه طلب العلم ، وأول ما حفظ متن الآجرومية» وسمع سائر الصحيح وكتاب «الشفا للقاضي عياض على الشيخ علي بن محمد العربي السقاط ، وحضر دروس أعيان عصره، واجتهد في التحصيل، ولازم دروس المالكي الشيخ العلامة علي بن أحمد الصعيدي العدوي المالكي، وهو شيخه في المعقول، قال عنه الأمير في ثبته: (لازمته له ما يفوق على عشرين سنة في كتب المعقول والمنقول إلى أن مات، ففي الحقيقة نسبتنا إليه، وجل انتفاعنا على يديه ، رضي الله تعالى عنه). وحضر على السيد الشيخ محمد البليدي شرحَ المحقق السعد على العقائد النسفية وغير ذلك وسمعَ «الموطأ» على هلال المغرب وعالمه الشيخ محمد سودة بالجامع الأزهر سنة ورُودِه بقصد الحج. التّاودي بن [؟] وتلقى عن حسن الجبرتي الفقه الحنفي وغير ذلك من الفنون الحكمية كالهيئة والهندسة والفلكيات والأوفاق عنه، وبواسطة تلميذه الشيخ محمد ابن إسمعيل النفراوي المالكي ، وكتب له إجازةً مُثبتةً في برنامج شيوخه. وحضر عند الشيخ يوسف الحفني في آداب البحث وبانت سعاد وعلى الشيخ محمد الحفني أخيه مجالس من الجامع الصغير» و«الشمائل» وعلى شيخ الإسلام أحمد الجوهري الكبير في شرح «الجوهرة» للشيخ عبد السلام . ومن شيوخه العالم المتفنن عطية الأجهوري، قال عنه في ثبته: حضرته في «المختصر لسعد الدين التفتازاني، وفي تفسير الجلالين وفي شيخ [؟])
Biography of the great scholar al-Amir al-Kabir, author of 'The Annotation on Ithaaf al-Mureed'. His name and lineage: He is the scholar, the shaykh Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Qadir ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Muhammad al-Sanbawi al-Maliki al-Azhari, famously known as al-Amir. Al-Jabarti said: The subject of the biography informed me in his own words that their origin was from the Maghrib; they settled in Egypt near Sayyidi Abd al-Wahhab Abi al-Takhsis, and they committed to a share in the district of 'Sanbu', and they moved there and settled there, and therein the subject of the biography was born. Where did the title 'al-Amir' come from? Al-Amir is the title of his grandfather Ahmad, and the reason is that Ahmad and his father Abd al-Qadir had amirate in the Sa'id, so the scholar al-Amir was called al-Amir al-Kabir (the Great Amir), and his son Muhammad after him was called al-Amir al-Saghir (the Lesser Amir). His birth, upbringing, pursuit of knowledge, and mention of some of his teachers. He was born in the month of Dhu al-Hijjah of the year one thousand one hundred and fifty-four (1154 AH). He received the Quran and its recitation from Shaykh Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Samnudi known as al-Munir. Love for seeking knowledge was instilled in him, and the first thing he memorized was the text of al-Ajrumiyyah, and he heard the rest of al-Sahih and the book 'al-Shifa' by Qadi Iyad from Shaykh Ali ibn Muhammad al-Arabi al-Saqqat. He attended the lessons of the leading figures of his time, and he strove hard in acquisition. He attended regularly the lessons of the Maliki scholar, the shaykh al-Allamah Ali ibn Ahmad al-Saidi al-Adawi al-Maliki, and he was his teacher in intellectual sciences. Al-Amir said about him in his Thabat: 'I attended him for more than twenty years in books of intellectual and transmitted sciences until he died. In truth, our affiliation is to him, and most of our benefit was at his hands, may Allah be pleased with him.' He attended under Sayyid al-Shaykh Muhammad al-Bilidi the commentary of al-Muhaqqiq al-Sa'd on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah and other things. And he heard 'al-Muwatta' from the prominent figure of the Maghrib and its scholar, Shaykh Muhammad Suda, at al-Azhar Mosque in the year of his arrival intending the Hajj. Al-Tawdi ibn [?] and he received Hanafi fiqh from Hasan al-Jabarti and other of the philosophical sciences such as astronomy, geometry, celestial matters, and talismanic squares from him, and through the intermediary of his student Shaykh Muhammad ibn Ismail al-Nafrawi al-Maliki, and he wrote for him a confirmed permission in the program of his teachers. And he attended under Shaykh Yusuf al-Hifni in Adab al-Bahth and Baanat Su'aad, and under Shaykh Muhammad al-Hifni, his brother, sessions of 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' and 'al-Shama'il', and under Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad al-Jawhari al-Kabir in the commentary on 'al-Jawhara' by Shaykh Abd al-Salam. And among his teachers was the polymath Atiyya al-Ujhuri, about whom he said in his Thabat: 'I attended him in al-Mukhtasar by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, and in Tafsir al-Jalalayn, and in Shaykh [؟]'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is a biographical passage introducing the author of the marginal commentary on Ithaaf al-Mureed, known as al-Amir al-Kabir. It begins with his full name and lineage, tracing to al-Sanbawi, a Maliki scholar from al-Azhar, famous as al-Amir. The text then clarifies the origin of the title 'al-Amir', explaining that it came from his grandfather Ahmad who held an amirate in Upper Egypt, leading to al-Amir being called 'al-Amir al-Kabir' and his son 'al-Amir al-Saghir'. The biography continues with his birth in 1154 AH, his early study of Quran recitation under al-Samnudi, and his memorization of the Ajrumiyyah. It then lists his teachers and studies: he heard Sahih al-Bukhari and al-Shifa under Ali al-Saqqat; attended lessons of contemporary scholars; and focused on the Maliki scholar Ali al-Saidi al-Adawi for over twenty years in both intellectual and transmitted sciences, considering him his primary teacher. He also studied under Muhammad al-Bilidi the commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah, heard al-Muwatta from Muhammad Suda, and received Hanafi fiqh and philosophical sciences from Hasan al-Jabarti, along with an ijaza. He attended sessions of adab and poetry under Yusuf al-Hifni and his brother, and studied al-Jawhara commentary under Ahmad al-Jawhari. Finally, he attended the polymath Atiyya al-Ujhuri in logic (al-Mukhtasar) and Quranic exegesis. The passage thus provides a detailed account of his educational background, emphasizing his mastery of both transmitted and rational sciences.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the title 'al-Amir' indicates royal lineage or princely birth.
Correction: The title actually stems from his grandfather and great-grandfather holding the administrative position of amir (governor) in Upper Egypt.

Checkpoint
Why was al-Amir al-Kabir given the title 'al-Amir'?
A) He was a prince by birth.
B) His grandfather and great-grandfather held an amirate in Upper Egypt.
C) He was the leader of a Sufi order.
D) He was the amir of the hajj caravan.

Key Takeaway
Al-Amir al-Kabir was a leading Maliki scholar of al-Azhar whose title derived from his family's administrative role and who studied under many prominent teachers in both transmitted and intellectual sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that al-Amir al-Kabir attended his teacher al-Adawi for over twenty years, dedicating himself to both transmitted and intellectual sciences. Which teacher or mentor in your life deserves that level of commitment from you? If you have none, what will you do to find one starting this week?
?
Al-Amir's love for seeking knowledge was instilled early, beginning with memorizing the Ajrumiyyah. What was the first Islamic text you memorized or studied deeply? Has that foundational knowledge faded from your memory? Write down one verse or hadith you memorized as a child and commit to reviewing it today.
?
Al-Amir studied under scholars of different disciplines—Maliki fiqh, Hanafi fiqh, astronomy, and more. Are there Islamic sciences or perspectives that you have avoided or dismissed? What specific subject will you learn more about to fulfill your duty as a seeker of truth, regardless of your comfort zone?

The Scholarly Lineage of al-Amir al-Kabir
Biography of al-Amir al-Kabir listing his teachers and studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of traditional Islamic education through the example of al-Amir al-Kabir's teachers and studies.

Core Idea
Scholarship in Islam is a chain of transmission from teacher to student.

This lesson introduces us to one of the great commentators on Ithaaf al-Mureed, al-Amir al-Kabir. Before studying his theological work, it is valuable to see the scholarly environment that shaped him. The passage below lists his teachers and the subjects he studied, offering a window into the traditional Islamic education system.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of al-Amir's teachers and studies.
Pay attention to the names of teachers and texts mentioned.
2
Identify the key teachers
List the teachers mentioned: al-‘Adawi, al-Balidi, Muhammad Sawda, al-Jabarti, al-Hifni brothers, al-Jawhari, and al-Ujhuri.
Each teacher specialized in different fields.
3
Notice the variety of subjects
Al-Amir studied rational sciences (ma‘qul), transmitted sciences (manqul), fiqh, tafsir, hadith, and even astronomy and geometry.
This shows the comprehensive nature of traditional Islamic education.
4
Reflect on the chain of transmission
The passage emphasizes that al-Amir 'attended for more than twenty years' with his main teacher, and that he received ijazat (licenses) from others.
This highlights the importance of continuous personal mentorship.

ترجمة الأمير الكبير صاحب الحاشية على إتحاف المريد. وكتاب «الشفا للقاضي عياض على الشيخ علي بن محمد العربي السقاط، وحضر دروس أعيان عصره، واجتهد في التحصيل، ولازم دروس المالكي الشيخ العلامة علي بن أحمد الصعيدي العدوي المالكي، وهو شيخه في المعقول، قال عنه الأمير في ثبته: (لازمته ما يفوق على عشرين سنة في كتب المعقول والمنقول إلى أن مات، ففي الحقيقة نسبتنا إليه، وجل انتفاعنا على يديه، رضي الله تعالى عنه). وحضر على السيد الشيخ محمد البليدي شرحَ المحقق السعد على العقائد النسفية وغير ذلك. وسمعَ «الموطأ» على هلال المغرب وعالمه الشيخ محمد سودة بالجامع الأزهر سنة ورُودِه بقصد الحج. والتقى عن حسن الجبرتي الفقه الحنفي وغير ذلك من الفنون الحكمية كالهيئة والهندسة والفلكيات والأوفاق عنه، وبواسطة تلميذه الشيخ محمد ابن إسمعيل النفراوي المالكي، وكتب له إجازةً مُثبتةً في برنامج شيوخه. وحضر عند الشيخ يوسف الحفني في آداب البحث وشرح بانت سعاد وعلى الشيخ محمد الحفني أخيه مجالس من الجامع الصغير» و«الشمائل» وعلى شيخ الإسلام أحمد الجوهري الكبير في شرح «الجوهرة» للشيخ عبد السلام. ومن شيوخه العالم المتفنن عطية الأجهوري، قال عنه في ثبته: حضرته في «المختصر لسعد الدين التفتازاني، وفي تفسير الجلالين وفي شرح شيخ الإسلام على الجزرية» وفي شرح سيدي محمد الزرقاني على البيقونية».
Biography of the great Amir, author of the commentary on Ithaaf al-Mureed. And the book 'al-Shifa' of Qadi Iyad with the commentary of Shaykh Ali ibn Muhammad al-Arabi al-Saqqat. He attended lessons of the eminent scholars of his time and strove in acquisition. He frequented the lessons of the Maliki scholar, the great scholar Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-Adawi al-Maliki, who was his teacher in rational sciences. Al-Amir said about him in his thabat: 'I attended his lessons for more than twenty years in books of rational and transmitted sciences until he died. So in reality our attribution is to him, and most of our benefit is through his hands, may Allah be pleased with him.' He attended with the sayyid shaykh Muhammad al-Balidi the commentary of the investigator al-Sa'd on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya and other things. He heard al-Muwatta' from the scholar of the Maghreb, the scholar Muhammad Sawda, at al-Azhar Mosque in the year of his arrival intending Hajj. He received from Hasan al-Jabarti Hanafi jurisprudence and other areas of philosophical sciences such as astronomy, geometry, celestial bodies, and numerical squares, through his student shaykh Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Nafrawi al-Maliki, and he wrote him a confirmed license (ijaza) in the program of his shaykhs. He attended with shaykh Yusuf al-Hifni in manners of research and the commentary on Banat Su'ad and with shaykh Muhammad al-Hifni, his brother, sessions on al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Shama'il, and with shaykh al-Islam Ahmad al-Jawhari al-Kabir on the commentary of al-Jawhara by shaykh Abd al-Salam. Among his shaykhs is the versatile scholar Atiyya al-Ujhuri, about whom he said in his thabat: 'I attended him in the Mukhtasar of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, and in Tafsir al-Jalalayn, and in the commentary of shaykh al-Islam on al-Jazariyya, and in the commentary of Sayyidi Muhammad al-Zurqani on al-Bayquniyya.'
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of the commentary on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It details his teachers and the subjects he studied. The passage begins by identifying the work: the biography of the author. It then lists his key teachers: Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-Adawi al-Maliki, his main teacher in rational sciences for over twenty years; Muhammad al-Balidi, with whom he studied al-Sa'd's commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya; Muhammad Sawda, from whom he heard al-Muwatta'; Hasan al-Jabarti, from whom he learned Hanafi jurisprudence and philosophical sciences; Yusuf al-Hifni; Muhammad al-Hifni; Ahmad al-Jawhari; and Atiyya al-Ujhuri. The passage mentions specific texts studied, such as al-Mukhtasar of al-Taftazani, Tafsir al-Jalalayn, and commentaries on al-Jazariyya, al-Jawhara, and al-Bayquniyya. The biography establishes al-Amir's scholarly lineage and breadth of knowledge.

Al-Amir's Fame, Teaching, and Students
Description of al-Amir's renown, teaching career, and praise from scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Amir al-Kabir's scholarly reputation grew to the point where even his teacher relied on his work, and how he became a leading teacher and authority.

Core Idea
A student's work became authoritative even for his own teacher.

This passage from the biography of al-Amir al-Kabir shows the remarkable trajectory of his scholarly career. It tells how he began teaching while his own teachers were still alive, and his teacher al-Adawi would consult al-Amir's own Mukhtasar when stumped. The passage also recounts his widespread fame, praise from scholars like al-Jabarti, and the many students who benefited from him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the narrative flow before analysing.
Notice the key terms like اشتهار and تصدر.
2
Identify the key anecdote
Find the story about al-Adawi asking for al-Amir's Mukhtasar. What does this tell you about al-Amir's standing?
This is a unique honor: a teacher using his student's work.
3
Reflect on the teacher-student dynamic
Think about how this anecdote challenges the usual assumption that the teacher is always the authority. How does it reflect Islamic ideals of knowledge?
4
Note the geographical reach
Observe that al-Amir's fame extended to the Maghreb, and the sultan sent him gifts. This shows his influence beyond Egypt.
5
Read al-Jabarti's praise
Read the passage where al-Jabarti describes al-Amir. What titles and qualities does he highlight?
This confirms his mastery in all sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشتهاره وتصدره للتدريس ومدح العلماء له: وبعد هذا التحصيل المُبارك وثني الرُّكب في مجالس الشيوخ والعلماء .. ظهرت عليه علامات المهارة والنجابة؛ فتصدر لإلقاء الدروس والتأليف في حياة شيوخه، وحكى الجبرتي ما يدل على ذلك فقال: كان شيخه العدوي إذا توقف في موضع يقول: (هاتوا مختصر الأمير) وهي منقبة شريفة. ونَما أمره، واشتهر فضله خصوصا بعد موت أشياخه، وشاع ذكره في الآفاق، وخصوصا بلاد المغرب، وكانت تأتيه الصلات من سلطان المغرب وتلك النواحي في كل عام، ووفد عليه الطالبون للأخذ عنه والتَّلقي منه، وتوجه في بعض المُقتضيات إلى دار السلطنة وألقى هناك دروسا حضرَ فيها علماؤهم، وشهدوا بفضله، واستجازوه وأجازهم بما هو مجاز به مِن أشياخه. قال عنه معاصره ـــ وهو ابن شيخه المذكور حسن الجبرتي - الشيخ المؤرخ عبد الرحمن الجبرتي: العالم العلّامة الفاضل الفهامة، صاحب التحقيقات الرائقة، والتأليفات الفائقة، شيخُ شيوخ أهل العلم، وصدرُ صُدورِ أهل الفهم، المُتفنّن في العلوم كلها، نقليّها وعقليّها وأدبيها، إليه انتهت الرياسة في العلوم بالديار المصرية، وبَاهَتْ مِصرُ ما سِواها بتحقيقاته البهية، استنبط الفروع من الأصول، واستخرج نفائس الدرر من بحور المعقول والمنقول. من تلاميذه: انتفع به الجم الغفير من العلماء وطلبة العلم، وبارك الله له في تلاميذه.
His fame and his taking the lead in teaching and the praise of scholars for him: After this blessed acquisition and kneeling in the sessions of shaykhs and scholars, signs of skill and success appeared on him, so he took the lead in delivering lessons and authoring works during the lifetime of his shaykhs. Al-Jabarti narrated what indicates that, saying: 'His teacher al-Adawi, if he paused at a point, would say: 'Bring me the Mukhtasar of al-Amir' — and this is an honorable distinction.' His affair grew and his virtue became famous, especially after the death of his shaykhs. His mention spread in the horizons, especially in the lands of the Maghreb. Gifts came to him from the Sultan of the Maghreb and those regions every year. Students came to him to take from him and receive from him. In some matters he went to the seat of the sultanate and gave lessons there which their scholars attended, and they testified to his virtue. They requested ijaza from him and he granted them what he was authorized to transmit from his shaykhs. His contemporary — and he is the son of his mentioned shaykh Hasan al-Jabarti — the historian shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Jabarti said about him: 'The all-knowing, most learned, excellent, most intelligent scholar; possessor of exquisite investigations and excellent compositions; shaykh of shaykhs of the people of knowledge; foremost of the foremost of the people of understanding; versatile in all sciences, transmitted, rational, and literary; to him ended leadership in the sciences in the Egyptian lands; Egypt boasted beyond others with his beautiful investigations; he derived branches from origins and extracted precious pearls from the seas of the rational and transmitted sciences.' Among his students: a great multitude of scholars and seekers of knowledge benefited from him, and Allah blessed him in his students.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage describes the fame, teaching career, and praise of al-Amir al-Kabir after his studies. It begins by stating that after his blessed acquisition of knowledge, he showed signs of skill and success. He began teaching and authoring works while his own teachers were still alive. The passage highlights a remarkable anecdote: his teacher al-Adawi, if he encountered a difficulty, would say 'bring me the Mukhtasar of al-Amir', showing that the student's work was authoritative even for the teacher. Al-Amir's fame increased after the death of his teachers, reaching distant regions, especially the Maghreb, where the sultan sent him annual gifts. Students flocked to him; he even traveled to the sultanate to teach, where local scholars attended and praised him. Then the historian Abd al-Rahman al-Jabarti is quoted giving a glowing description, calling him versatile in all sciences and saying that leadership in knowledge ended with him in Egypt. Finally, the passage notes that a vast multitude of scholars and students benefited from him and were blessed.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A student cannot surpass or become more authoritative than his own teacher.
Correction: This anecdote shows that in Islam, knowledge is respected regardless of age or status. A student's work can become a reference even for the teacher, as al-Adawi used al-Amir's Mukhtasar.

Checkpoint
What did al-Adawi, al-Amir's teacher, do when he paused at a difficulty?
A) He asked al-Amir for help
B) He requested the Mukhtasar of al-Amir
C) He stopped teaching
D) He consulted other scholars

Key Takeaway
Al-Amir's scholarship was so esteemed that even his teacher relied on his Mukhtasar, demonstrating that knowledge is measured by merit, not position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you, as a student, produced work that your own teacher could rely on? What would it take for you to reach that level of mastery that even your mentors benefit from your efforts?
?
Al-Amir's fame came after years of dedicated study and humility (kneeling before shaykhs). Are you willing to spend years in obscurity, learning, before seeking recognition? Or do you desire fame before substance?
?
His teacher al-Adawi was not too proud to admit his need for his student's work. Is there someone you look down upon from whom you could actually learn? What pride is holding you back from benefiting from those you consider beneath you?

The Fame and Teaching of al-Amir al-Kabir
Biographical narrative of al-Amir's fame and scholarly praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Amir al-Kabir rose to prominence as a scholar and the recognition he received from his peers and rulers.

Core Idea
Al-Amir al-Kabir's mastery was so recognized that even his teacher relied on his work.

This passage from the biographical tradition recounts the remarkable career of al-Amir al-Kabir, a scholar whose expertise commanded respect even from his own teachers. After completing his studies, he became a leading teacher and author while his shaykhs were still alive. The historian al-Jabarti records a telling anecdote and provides a glowing tribute that captures his towering status in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice the sequence: studies → signs of skill → teaching → fame → students → travel → praise.
Pay attention to the anecdote about al-‘Adawī asking for the Mukhtaṣar.
2
Identify key events
List the major events in al-Amir's life as described: his becoming prominent for teaching, the anecdote with his shaykh, the spread of fame to the Maghrib, and his journey to the sultanate.
Each event shows a different aspect of his recognition.
3
Analyze the praise from al-Jabarti
Examine the eulogy: what titles does al-Jabarti use? What accomplishments does he highlight? This shows how contemporaries viewed him.
The praise is from a respected historian, adding credibility.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why would a teacher rely on a student's work? What does this say about al-Amir's intellectual contributions?
This connects to the lesson's core idea.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشتهاره وتصدره للتدريس ومدح العلماء له:
وبعد هذا التحصيل المُبارك وثني الرُّكب في مجالس الشيوخ والعلماء .. ظهرت عليه علامات المهارة والنجابة ; فتصدر لإلقاء الدروس والتأليف في حياة شيوخه، وحكى الجبرتي ما يدل على ذلك فقال: كان شيخه العدوي إذا توقف في موضع يقول : (هاتوا مختصر الأمير) وهي منقبة شريفة . ونَما أمره ، واشتهر فضله خصوصا بعد موت أشياخه ، وشاع ذكره في الآفاق ، وخصوصا بلاد المغرب، وكانت تأتيه الصلات من سلطان المغرب وتلك النواحي في كل عام، ووفد عليه الطالبون للأخذ عنه والتَّلقي منه، وتوجه في بعض المُقتضيات إلى دار السلطنة وألقى هناك دروسا حضرَ فيها علماؤهم ، وشهدوا بفضله، واستجازوه وأجازهم بما هو مجاز به مِن أشياخه
.
قال عنه معاصره ـــ وهو ابن شيخه المذكور حسن الجبرتي - الشيخ المؤرخ عبد الرحمن الجبرتي : العالم العلّامة الفاضل الفهامة، صاحب التحقيقات الرائقة ، والتأليفات الفائقة ، شيخُ شيوخ أهل العلم، وصدرُ صُدورِ أهل الفهم، المُتفنّن في العلوم كلها ، نقليّها وعقليّها وأدبيها ، إليه انتهت الرياسة في العلوم بالديار المصرية ، وبَاهَتْ مِصرُ ما سِواها بتحقيقاته البهية، استنبط الفروع من الأصول، واستخرج نفائس الدرر من بحور المعقول والمنقول .
His fame, becoming prominent for teaching, and scholars' praise for him: And after this blessed acquisition and bending the knees in the gatherings of shaykhs and scholars, signs of skill and excellence appeared upon him; so he became prominent for delivering lessons and authoring works during the lifetime of his shaykhs. Al-Jabarti narrated what indicates that, saying: His shaykh al-‘Adawī, whenever he paused at a place, would say: 'Bring the Mukhtaṣar of al-Amīr' — and this is a noble honor. His reputation grew, and his excellence became famous especially after the death of his shaykhs, and his mention spread in the horizons, especially the lands of the Maghrib. Gifts used to come to him from the Sultan of Morocco and those regions every year. Students flocked to him to learn and receive from him. He went on some official matters to the seat of the sultanate and there delivered lessons attended by their scholars, who witnessed his excellence and sought his permission (ijāzah), and he granted them ijāzah for what he himself was authorized by his shaykhs. His contemporary—who is the son of his aforementioned shaykh Ḥasan al-Jabartī—the historian Shaykh ‘Abd al-Raḥmān al-Jabartī said about him: 'The scholar, all-‘allāmah, excellent, very intelligent, possessor of brilliant investigations and superior compositions, the shaykh of shaykhs of the people of knowledge, the foremost of the foremost of the people of understanding, versatile in all sciences—both transmitted and rational and literary—to him ended the leadership in the sciences in the Egyptian lands. Egypt boasted over others because of his fine investigations. He derived branches from fundamentals and extracted precious pearls from the seas of reason and transmitted knowledge.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of al-Amir al-Kabir's rise to fame and the praise he received from scholars. It begins by describing how after his studies, signs of skill appeared, and he began teaching and writing while his own teachers were still alive. It recounts an anecdote from al-Jabarti: his teacher al-‘Adawī, when stuck, would ask for al-Amir's Mukhtaṣar, indicating the teacher's reliance on him. Then it describes the growth of his reputation, especially after his teachers' deaths, and his fame spreading to the Maghrib, with the Sultan sending gifts and students coming to learn. It also mentions a trip to the seat of the sultanate where he taught and was recognized. The passage ends with a long eulogy from the historian al-Jabarti, praising his comprehensive knowledge and leadership in Egypt.

The Illustrious Students of al-Amir al-Kabir
Enumeration of al-Amir al-Kabir's notable students.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key students of al-Amir al-Kabir and their contributions to Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Amir al-Kabir's students shaped Islamic scholarship for generations.

Al-Amir al-Kabir's genius extended beyond his own works; he nurtured a generation of luminaries who became pillars of Islamic learning. This passage lists his most famous students, many of whom became Shaykhs of al-Azhar and authored enduring works. Let's explore each one's legacy.

From his students: A large crowd of scholars and students benefited from him, and Allah blessed him in his students, so they became among the great scholars and shaykhs of al-Azhar. Among them: 1. The all-‘allāmah Aḥmad al-Ṣāwī, author of the famous Ḥāshiyah on Tafsīr al-Jalālayn. - His son al-Amīr al-Ṣaghīr, who is Muḥammad al-Ṣaghīr, and he is Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad Aḥmad ibn al-Sanbāwī. - And Shaykh Muḥammad Amīn ‘Ābidīn al-Ḥanafī, author of the famous Ḥāshiyah. - And Shaykh Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī al-Damhūjī, Shaykh al-Azhar in his time. - And Shaykh Ḥasan al-Quwaysnī, Shaykh al-Azhar in his time. - And the all-‘allāmah Ibrāhīm al-Bājūrī, Shaykh al-Azhar, author of Ḥawāshī and books. - And Shaykh Ḥasan al-‘Adawī al-Ḥamzāwī, author of the book 'Irshād al-Murīd' in creed. - And among his students is the father of the muḥaddith of the Syrian lands, the all-‘allāmah Badr al-Dīn al-Ḥasanī, Shaykh Yūsuf Badr al-Dīn al-Maghribī then al-Dimashqī. And many others.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage lists the notable students of al-Amir al-Kabir. It begins by stating that a large crowd benefited from him, and Allah blessed his students, many becoming major scholars and shaykhs of al-Azhar. Then it enumerates eight individuals: 1) Aḥmad al-Ṣāwī, known for his supercommentary on Tafsīr al-Jalālayn. Also mentioned is his son Muḥammad al-Ṣaghīr. 2) Muḥammad Amīn ‘Ābidīn al-Ḥanafī, famous for his Ḥāshiyah. 3) Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī al-Damhūjī, a former Shaykh al-Azhar. 4) Ḥasan al-Quwaysnī, another Shaykh al-Azhar. 5) Ibrāhīm al-Bājūrī, also a Shaykh al-Azhar and author of glosses. 6) Ḥasan al-‘Adawī al-Ḥamzāwī, author of a creedal work 'Irshād al-Murīd'. 7) Yūsuf Badr al-Dīn al-Maghribī, father of the famous muḥaddith Badr al-Dīn al-Ḥasanī. The list shows the wide influence of al-Amir al-Kabir.

Al-Amir al-Kabir's Work: al-Majmū‘
Lists one of al-Amir al-Kabir's works and its description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand one of al-Amir al-Kabir's major works, al-Majmū‘, and its commentary.

Core Idea
Al-Majmū‘ is a concise legal work modeled after Mukhtaṣar Khalīl.

This lesson introduces one of the key works of al-Amir al-Kabir, a prominent 19th-century Maliki scholar. The passage describes his book al-Majmū‘, a concise legal text, and mentions the commentary he wrote on it. Understanding his scholarly output helps appreciate his contribution to Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

3

Teachers and Student of al-Amir al-Kabir
Listing teachers and a student of al-Amir al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage of al-Amir al-Kabir through his teachers and his influence on a prominent student.

Core Idea
A scholar's teachers and students shape his legacy.

This passage introduces us to the network of scholars surrounding al-Amir al-Kabir. By learning who taught him and who learned from him, we see his position in the Azhar tradition. The list of seven teachers includes some of the most famous names of the era, and the one student mentioned became a leading hadith scholar in Syria.

Guided Path
1
Read the teacher list
Read the list of seven teachers, noting their titles like 'Shaykh of al-Azhar' and their famous works. This shows the caliber of scholars al-Amir studied under.
The list begins with 'from among them' (منهم), indicating it is not exhaustive.
2
Identify the student
Find the name of the student mentioned and his connection to Syrian hadith scholarship. The phrase 'and many others' reminds us this is just one example.
3
Reflect on selectivity
Understand that the phrase 'among them' and 'and many others' indicates this is a selection, not a complete list. This helps avoid the misconception that these are the only teachers and students.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الأمير الكبير صاحب الحاشية على إتحاف المريد

فأصبحوا من كبار العلماء، وشيوخ الأزهر، ومنهم:

۱ - العلامة أحمد الصاوي صاحب الحاشية المشهورة على تفسير الجلالين.
- ولده الأمير الصغير، وهو محمد الصغير، وهو محمد بن محمد بن محمد أحمد بن السنباوي.
٣ - والشيخ محمد أمين عابدين الحنفي، صاحب الحاشية المشهور.
٤ - والشيخ أحمد بن علي الدمهوجي شيخ الأزهر في عصره.
ه - والشيخ حسن القويسني شيخ الأزهر في عصره.
٦ ـ والعلامة إبراهيم الباجوري شيخ الأزهر صاحب الحواشي والكتب.
۷ - والشيخ حسن العدوي الحمزاوي صاحب كتاب «إرشاد المريد» في العقيدة.

ومن تلاميذه والد محدث الديار الشامية العلامة بدر الدين الحسنى الشيخ يوسف بدر الدين المغربي ثم الدمشقي. وغيرهم كثير.

من مؤلفاته

۱ - كتاب «المجموع» وهو من أبرز ما صنف، حاكي في اختصاره وحصر مسائله «مختصر خليل» وله عليه شرح سماه: «ضوء الشموع على شرح المجموع» وهو المختصر الذي كان يطلبه شيخه العدوي إذا توقف في مسألة بقوله: هاتوا مختصر الأمير. وقد شرحه العلامة عليش المالكي بشرح حافل سماه: «مواهب القدير في شرح مجموع الأمير» وله نسخ مخطوطة عدة في المكتبة الأزهرية.

۲ - وله شرح على مختصر خليل سماه الإكليل في شرح مختصر خليل.

۳ - وله في العقيدة: كفاية المريد وغنية الطالب للتوحيد.

٤ ـ وحاشية على إتحاف المريد للشيخ عبد السلام، وهي الحاشية التي استعنا بها كثيرا في شرح عبارات وحل مشكلات إتحاف المريد في عملنا هذا، وقد انتهى العلامة الأمير من تأليفها سنة: (١١٨٥ هـ).

ه - وله في مسائل الكلامية: «مَطْلَعُ النَّبِرَيْنِ فيما يتعلق بالقُدْرَتَيْن» وقد طبعت حديثا بتحقيق الشيخ الفاضل محمود صادق الحساني عن دار النور المبين الأردنية ولها طبعة مغربية أخرى صدرت عن الرابطة المحمدية للعلماء سنة: (٢٠١٦) بتحقيق الدكتور يوسف الحزيمري.

۷ - وله في البلاغة حاشية على شرح الملوي على السمرقندية.

۸ - وله في آداب فهم العبارة وإفهامها «ثَمَرُ الثَّمَام شرح غاية الإحكام في آداب الفهم والإفهام».

۹ - وله في الأحاديث الموضوعة النخبة البهية في الأحاديث المكذوبة على خير البرية.

۱۰ - ورسالة إتحافُ الإِنْسِ في الفرق بين اسم الجنس وعلم الجنس.
Translation of the great Amir, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. So they became among the great scholars and shaykhs of al-Azhar, and among them: 1- The learned Ahmad al-Sawi, author of the famous gloss on the Tafsir of al-Jalalayn. - His son the minor Amir, who is Muhammad al-Saghir, and he is Muhammad bin Muhammad bin Muhammad Ahmad bin al-Sanbawi. 3- And Shaykh Muhammad Amin Abidin al-Hanafi, author of the famous gloss. 4- And Shaykh Ahmad bin Ali al-Damhuji, Shaykh of al-Azhar in his time. 5- And Shaykh Hasan al-Quwaysini, Shaykh of al-Azhar in his time. 6- And the learned Ibrahim al-Bajuri, Shaykh of al-Azhar, author of glosses and books. 7- And Shaykh Hasan al-Adawi al-Hamzawi, author of the book 'Irshad al-Mureed' on creed. And among his students: the father of the hadith scholar of Syria, the learned Badr al-Din al-Hasani, Shaykh Yusuf Badr al-Din al-Maghribi then al-Dimashqi, and many others. From his works: 1- The book 'al-Majmu' which is among the most prominent of what he authored, emulating in its conciseness and comprehensiveness 'Mukhtasar Khalil', and he has a commentary on it called 'Daw' al-Shumu' ala Sharh al-Majmu', and it is the compendium that his teacher al-Adawi used to request when he hesitated on a matter by saying: 'Bring the compendium of al-Amir.' And the learned Ulaysh al-Maliki commented on it with a comprehensive commentary called 'Mawahib al-Qadir fi Sharh Majmu' al-Amir', and there are several manuscript copies in the Azhar library. 2- And he has a commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil called 'al-Iklil fi Sharh Mukhtasar Khalil'. 3- And he has on creed: 'Kifayat al-Mureed wa Ghunyat al-Talib li al-Tawhid'. 4- And a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed by Shaykh Abd al-Salam, and it is the gloss that we have used extensively in explaining phrases and solving problems of Ithaaf al-Mureed in this work of ours, and the learned al-Amir finished its authorship in the year 1185 AH. 5- And he has on theological issues: 'Matla' al-Nabirayn fima Yata'allaq bi al-Qudratayn', and it has been recently printed under the editing of the virtuous Shaykh Mahmud Sadiq al-Hasani from Dar al-Nur al-Mubin al-Urduniyya, and it has another Moroccan edition published by al-Rabita al-Muhammadiyya li al-'Ulama in the year 2016, edited by Dr. Yusuf al-Huzaymiri. 7- And he has on rhetoric a gloss on Sharh al-Mallawi on al-Samarqandiyya. 8- And he has on the etiquette of understanding and conveying expression 'Thamar al-Thamam Sharh Ghayat al-Ihkam fi Adab al-Fahm wa al-Ifham'. 9- And he has on fabricated hadiths: 'al-Nukhba al-Bahiyya fi al-Ahadith al-Makdhouba 'ala Khayr al-Bariyya'. 10- And the treatise 'Ithaf al-Insi fi al-Farq bayna Ism al-Jins wa 'Ilm al-Jins'.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice (tarjama) of the scholar known as al-Amir al-Kabir, who authored the gloss on the poem Ithaaf al-Mureed. The biography proceeds in three parts: first, a list of his teachers; second, a note on his students; third, a catalogue of his major works. The teachers are seven named individuals, each introduced by a number or dash, all of whom were prominent Azhar shaykhs or scholars. They include Ahmad al-Sawi (known for his gloss on Tafsir al-Jalalayn), his own son Muhammad al-Saghir, Muhammad Amin Abidin al-Hanafi, Ahmad al-Damhuji, Hasan al-Quwaysini, Ibrahim al-Bajuri, and Hasan al-Adawi al-Hamzawi. The student mentioned is Yusuf Badr al-Din al-Maghribi, a hadith scholar of Syria, along with the phrase 'and many others'. The works section lists ten items: first, 'al-Majmu', a compendium emulating Mukhtasar Khalil with its own commentary; second, a commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil called 'al-Iklil'; third, a creedal work 'Kifayat al-Mureed'; fourth, the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed itself, noting its completion date of 1185 AH; fifth, a theological work on two powers; sixth (missing number but likely seventh), a rhetorical gloss; eighth, a work on the etiquette of understanding and expression; ninth, a work on fabricated hadiths; tenth, a treatise on the difference between ism al-jins and 'ilm al-jins. The passage thus provides a concise scholarly biography, emphasizing al-Amir's connections and contributions.

?

Major Works of al-Amir al-Kabir
Listing the major works of al-Amir al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth and significance of al-Amir al-Kabir's scholarly works, especially his gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed.

Core Idea
Al-Amir al-Kabir authored works spanning fiqh, creed, rhetoric, and hadith, with his gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed being central to our study.

This passage catalogues ten works by al-Amir al-Kabir, covering multiple Islamic sciences. The list reveals his expertise in jurisprudence (especially the Maliki school), theology, rhetoric, and hadith criticism. The gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed is highlighted as a key resource for this course, completed in 1185 AH.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list of works
Read through the ten works to get a sense of the subjects covered: fiqh, creed, rhetoric, hadith, and language.
Notice the first work 'al-Majmu' is given the most attention.
2
Identify the fiqh works
The first two works (al-Majmu and al-Iklil) are commentaries on Maliki fiqh texts. Understand their relationship to Mukhtasar Khalil.
3
Note the creedal works
Works three and four are on creed: Kifayat al-Mureed and the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. The gloss is the focus of this course and its completion date is given.
4
Appreciate the diversity
The remaining works cover theology, rhetoric, hadith criticism, and language. This shows al-Amir al-Kabir's comprehensive scholarship.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الأمير الكبير صاحب الحاشية على إتحاف المريد

فأصبحوا من كبار العلماء، وشيوخ الأزهر، ومنهم:

۱ - العلامة أحمد الصاوي صاحب الحاشية المشهورة على تفسير الجلالين.
- ولده الأمير الصغير، وهو محمد الصغير، وهو محمد بن محمد بن محمد أحمد بن السنباوي.
٣ - والشيخ محمد أمين عابدين الحنفي، صاحب الحاشية المشهور.
٤ - والشيخ أحمد بن علي الدمهوجي شيخ الأزهر في عصره.
ه - والشيخ حسن القويسني شيخ الأزهر في عصره.
٦ ـ والعلامة إبراهيم الباجوري شيخ الأزهر صاحب الحواشي والكتب.
۷ - والشيخ حسن العدوي الحمزاوي صاحب كتاب «إرشاد المريد» في العقيدة.

ومن تلاميذه والد محدث الديار الشامية العلامة بدر الدين الحسنى الشيخ يوسف بدر الدين المغربي ثم الدمشقي. وغيرهم كثير.

من مؤلفاته

۱ - كتاب «المجموع» وهو من أبرز ما صنف، حاكي في اختصاره وحصر مسائله «مختصر خليل» وله عليه شرح سماه: «ضوء الشموع على شرح المجموع» وهو المختصر الذي كان يطلبه شيخه العدوي إذا توقف في مسألة بقوله: هاتوا مختصر الأمير. وقد شرحه العلامة عليش المالكي بشرح حافل سماه: «مواهب القدير في شرح مجموع الأمير» وله نسخ مخطوطة عدة في المكتبة الأزهرية.

۲ - وله شرح على مختصر خليل سماه الإكليل في شرح مختصر خليل.

۳ - وله في العقيدة: كفاية المريد وغنية الطالب للتوحيد.

٤ ـ وحاشية على إتحاف المريد للشيخ عبد السلام، وهي الحاشية التي استعنا بها كثيرا في شرح عبارات وحل مشكلات إتحاف المريد في عملنا هذا، وقد انتهى العلامة الأمير من تأليفها سنة: (١١٨٥ هـ).

ه - وله في مسائل الكلامية: «مَطْلَعُ النَّبِرَيْنِ فيما يتعلق بالقُدْرَتَيْن» وقد طبعت حديثا بتحقيق الشيخ الفاضل محمود صادق الحساني عن دار النور المبين الأردنية ولها طبعة مغربية أخرى صدرت عن الرابطة المحمدية للعلماء سنة: (٢٠١٦) بتحقيق الدكتور يوسف الحزيمري.

۷ - وله في البلاغة حاشية على شرح الملوي على السمرقندية.

۸ - وله في آداب فهم العبارة وإفهامها «ثَمَرُ الثَّمَام شرح غاية الإحكام في آداب الفهم والإفهام».

۹ - وله في الأحاديث الموضوعة النخبة البهية في الأحاديث المكذوبة على خير البرية.

۱۰ - ورسالة إتحافُ الإِنْسِ في الفرق بين اسم الجنس وعلم الجنس.
Translation of the great Amir, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. So they became among the great scholars and shaykhs of al-Azhar, and among them: 1- The learned Ahmad al-Sawi, author of the famous gloss on the Tafsir of al-Jalalayn. - His son the minor Amir, who is Muhammad al-Saghir, and he is Muhammad bin Muhammad bin Muhammad Ahmad bin al-Sanbawi. 3- And Shaykh Muhammad Amin Abidin al-Hanafi, author of the famous gloss. 4- And Shaykh Ahmad bin Ali al-Damhuji, Shaykh of al-Azhar in his time. 5- And Shaykh Hasan al-Quwaysini, Shaykh of al-Azhar in his time. 6- And the learned Ibrahim al-Bajuri, Shaykh of al-Azhar, author of glosses and books. 7- And Shaykh Hasan al-Adawi al-Hamzawi, author of the book 'Irshad al-Mureed' on creed. And among his students: the father of the hadith scholar of Syria, the learned Badr al-Din al-Hasani, Shaykh Yusuf Badr al-Din al-Maghribi then al-Dimashqi, and many others. From his works: 1- The book 'al-Majmu' which is among the most prominent of what he authored, emulating in its conciseness and comprehensiveness 'Mukhtasar Khalil', and he has a commentary on it called 'Daw' al-Shumu' ala Sharh al-Majmu', and it is the compendium that his teacher al-Adawi used to request when he hesitated on a matter by saying: 'Bring the compendium of al-Amir.' The Scholarly Output of al-Amir al-Kabir
Enumerates the twelve major works of al-Amir al-Kabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth and diversity of al-Amir al-Kabir's scholarly works across multiple Islamic disciplines.

Core Idea
One scholar, twelve works spanning fiqh, kalam, balaghah, hadith, and language.

This passage is a biographical sketch that enumerates the major works of al-Amir al-Kabir, the renowned author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. As you read through the list, notice the variety of subjects he wrote on, from creed and theology to rhetoric and linguistics. This overview sets the stage for appreciating his scholarly stature and the depth of his contributions.

Guided Path
1
Read the complete list of works
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the twelve numbered entries. Observe the range of titles and the brief descriptions.
2
Group the works by field
Identify which work belongs to which discipline: fiqh, creed (aqidah), kalam, balaghah, hadith, language, and biographical records (thabat).
For example, item 2 is in fiqh, item 3 in creed, item 5 in kalam.
3
Reflect on the scholar’s methodology
Notice that many works are commentaries (sharh) or glosses (hashiyah), indicating a tradition of building upon earlier texts. Also note that the biographer acknowledges this is not exhaustive.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الأمير الكبير صاحب الحاشية على إتحاف

مسألة بقوله : هاتوا مختصر الأمير». وقد شرحه العلامة عليش المالكي بشرح حافل سماه: «مواهب القدير في شرح مجموع الأمير» وله نسخ مخطوطة عدة في المكتبة الأزهرية.

٢ - وله شرح على مختصر خليل سماه الإكليل في شرح مختصر خليل».

٣ - وله في العقيدة: كفاية المريد وغنية الطالب للتوحيد».

٤ ـ وحاشية على إتحاف المريد للشيخ عبد السلام، وهي الحاشية استعنا بها كثيرا في شرح عبارات وحل مشكلات إتحاف المريد في عملنا هذا، وقد انتهى العلامة الأمير من تأليفها سنة : (١١٨٥ هـ).

ه وله في مسائل الكلامية: «مَطْلَعُ النَّبِرَيْنِ فيما يتعلق بالقُدْرتَيْن» وقد طبعت حديثا بتحقيق الشيخ الفاضل محمود صادق الحساني عن دار النور المبين الأردنية ولها طبعة مغربية أخرى صدرت عن الرابطة المحمدية للعلماء سنة : (٢٠١٦) بتحقيق الدكتور يوسف الحزيمري .

٦ - وله في البلاغة حاشية على شرح الملوي على السمرقندية .

۷ - وله في آداب فهم العبارة وإفهامها «ثَمَرُ الثَّمَام شرح غاية الإحكام في آداب الفهم والإفهام .

۸ - وله في الأحاديث الموضوعة النخبة البهية في الأحاديث المكذوبة على خير البرية .

۹ - ورسالة إتحافُ الإِنْسِ في الفرق بين اسم الجنس وعلم الجنس .

۱۰ - وله حاشية نافعة على مغني اللبيب».

۱۱ - سد الأرب من علو الإسناد والأدب وهو ثَبتُه .

۱۲ ـ وحاشية على شرح شذور الذهب وغير ذلك من الكتب والحواشي والتحقيقات النافعة، حيث لم نُرد حصر مؤلفاته في هذه الترجمة المختصرة المُستعجلة .
Biography of al-Amir al-Kabir, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed.

A question (mas'alah) with his saying: 'Bring me the Mukhtasar of al-Amir.' And the scholar 'Alaysh al-Maliki explained it with a comprehensive commentary named 'Mawahib al-Qadir fi Sharh Majmu' al-Amir' and it has several manuscript copies in the Azhar Library.

2 - And he has a commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil named al-Iklil fi Sharh Mukhtasar Khalil.

3 - And he has in creed (al-'aqidah): Kifayat al-Mureed wa Ghunyat al-Talib li al-Tawhid.

4 - And a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed by Shaykh 'Abd al-Salam, and that is the gloss we relied on much in explaining phrases and solving problems of Ithaaf al-Mureed in this our work, and the scholar al-Amir finished its authorship in the year 1185 AH.

5 - And he has in theological issues (al-masa'il al-kalamiyyah): 'Matla' al-Nabirayn fima Yata'allaq bi al-Qudratayn' and it was printed recently under the editing of the virtuous Shaykh Mahmud Sadiq al-Hasani from Dar al-Nur al-Mubin al-Urduniyyah, and it has another Moroccan edition published by al-Rabitah al-Muhammadiyyah li al-'Ulama' in the year 2016 under the editing of Dr. Yusuf al-Hazimiri.

6 - And he has in rhetoric (al-balaghah) a gloss on Sharh al-Mallawi 'ala al-Samarqandiyyah.

7 - And he has in the etiquettes of understanding expression and making it understood: 'Thamar al-Thamam Sharh Ghayat al-Ihkam fi Adab al-Fahm wa al-Ifham.'

8 - And he has on fabricated hadiths: al-Nukhbah al-Bahiyyah fi al-Ahadith al-Makdhubah 'ala Khayr al-Bariyyah.

9 - And a treatise: Ithaaf al-Ins fi al-Farq bayn Ism al-Jins wa 'Ilm al-Jins.

10 - And he has a beneficial gloss on Mughni al-Labib.

11 - Sadd al-Arab min 'Uluww al-Isnad wa al-Adab, and it is his thabat (index of teachers).

12 - And a gloss on Sharh Shudhur al-Dhahab, and other beneficial books, glosses, and critical editions, for we did not intend to enumerate his works in this brief and hasty biography.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list that enumerates the major works of al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins with the heading 'Biography of al-Amir al-Kabir.' The first item describes a work that was questioned, and that the scholar 'Alaysh al-Maliki wrote a commentary on it. Then the list proceeds with twelve numbered entries. Each entry provides the title and brief details: item 2 is a commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil in Maliki fiqh; item 3 is a theological work on tawhid; item 4 is the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed itself, which the biographer notes as the main reference for this work; item 5 is a theological work on divine power; item 6 is a rhetorical gloss; item 7 is on the adab of understanding and conveying meaning; item 8 is on fabricated hadiths; item 9 is a treatise on linguistic distinctions; item 10 is a gloss on Ibn Hisham's Mughni al-Labib; item 11 is his thabat (academic index); item 12 is a gloss on a grammatical work. The biographer ends by acknowledging that this list is not exhaustive. The passage demonstrates the vast scope of al-Amir's scholarship across fiqh, kalam, balaghah, hadith, language, and other fields.

Correction: It is a separate biographical sketch of the glossator, not a table of contents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Amir al-Kabir authored at least twelve works across multiple sciences while also teaching and writing glosses. What is your own contribution to preserving and spreading sacred knowledge? Will you rise to even a fraction of his dedication, or settle for passively consuming content?

?
The gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed was completed in 1185 AH and is still studied today. What will you leave behind that will benefit others after you die? Is your daily effort building anything that outlasts you?

Al-Amir al-Kabir: Character and Death
Describes al-Amir's gentle character, illness, death date, burial, and his scholarly son.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the character, final illness, and death of al-Amir al-Kabir, as well as his scholarly legacy through his son.

Core Idea
A gentle scholar whose life ended in illness but whose legacy lived on through his son.

This passage offers a personal glimpse into the life of al-Amir al-Kabir, focusing on his gentle disposition, his final illness, and his death. It also highlights the continuation of his scholarly lineage through his son, Muhammad al-Amir al-Saghir. As you read, notice the vivid description of his sensitivity and the respect he commanded, evident from the packed funeral.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand the meaning.
2
Identify character traits
Find the phrases that describe al-Amir's personality: 'رقيق القلب', 'لطيف المزاج', etc. Notice how his sensitivity is depicted.
The phrase 'ينزعج طبعه من غير انزعاج' is key.
3

Date: Monday, 10th Dhu al-Qa'dah 1232 AH.
4

5

The son continues the scholarly tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفاته

وكان رقيق القلب، لطيف المزاج ، ينزعج طبعه من غير انزعاج، يكاد الوهم يؤلمه، وسماعُ المُنافِر يُوهِنه ويُسقمه، وبآخره ضعفت قواه، وتراخت اعضاؤه ، وزاد شكواه ، ولم يزل يتعلل والأمراض به تسلسل ، وداعي المنون عنه لا يتحول إلى أن توفي يوم الاثنين عاشر ذي القعدة الحرام من سنة اثنين وثلاثين ومئتين بعد الألف (۱۲۳۲) هـ) وكان له مشهد حافل، ودفن بالصحراء بجوار مدفن الشيخ عبد الوهاب العفيفي بالقرب من عمارة السلطان قايتباي وكثُرَ عليه الأسف والحُزن ، وخلف وَلَدُه العلامة التحرير الشيخ محمد الأمير الصغير ، وكان كوالده أحد الصدور يقرأ الدروس ويفيد الطلبة ويحضر الدواوين والمجالس العالية
His Death

And he was tender-hearted, gentle in temperament, his nature would be disturbed without agitation, imagination almost pained him, and hearing what was discordant weakened him and made him ill. And at the end his strength weakened, his limbs became lax, and his complaint increased. He continued to ail, and illnesses followed him in succession, and the call of death did not cease from him until he died on Monday, the tenth of Dhu al-Qa'dah al-Haram of the year one thousand two hundred and thirty-two (1232 AH). And he had a packed funeral procession, and was buried in the desert next to the tomb of Shaykh 'Abd al-Wahhab al-'Afifi near the building of Sultan Qaytbay. And sorrow and grief were abundant over him. And he left behind his son, the erudite scholar Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir al-Saghir, who was like his father, one of the prominent figures, teaching lessons, benefiting students, and attending offices and high assemblies.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a biographical description of the character and death of al-Amir al-Kabir. It begins with the heading 'His Death.' Then it describes his personality: he was tender-hearted, gentle, easily affected by imagination and discordant sounds. It then narrates his declining health: his strength waned, his limbs weakened, his complaints increased, and diseases followed one another until death came to him on Monday, 10th Dhu al-Qa'dah 1232 AH. The funeral was crowded, and he was buried in the desert near the tomb of Shaykh 'Abd al-Wahhab al-'Afifi, close to Sultan Qaytbay's building. The biographer notes the profound grief felt at his passing. Finally, it mentions his legacy: his son, Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir al-Saghir, who became a great scholar like his father, teaching, benefiting students, and attending scholarly councils. The passage thus covers his moral qualities, his final illness, the date and circumstances of his death, and the continuation of his scholarly line through his son.

Key Terms
رقيق القلب
المنون
مشهد حافل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'ينزعج طبعه من غير انزعاج' is contradictory, meaning he was disturbed without being disturbed.
Correction: It actually means he was sensitive and easily affected inwardly, but he did not show outward agitation or disturbance.
